				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase_%26_Co.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co.">JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co.</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co. For its main subsidiaries, see <a href="/wiki/Chase_Bank" title="Chase Bank">Chase Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/J.P._Morgan_%26_Co." title="J.P. Morgan &amp; Co.">J.P. Morgan &amp; Co.</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the company. For the person, see <a href="/wiki/J._P._Morgan" title="J. P. Morgan">J. P. Morgan</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co.</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/Investment_banking" title="Investment banking">investment bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a> <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a> headquartered in <a href="/wiki/City_of_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="City of New York">New York City</a>. JPMorgan Chase is ranked by <a href="/wiki/S%26P_Global" title="S&amp;P Global">S&amp;P Global</a> as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_banks_in_the_United_States" title="List of largest banks in the United States">largest bank in the United States</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_banks" title="List of largest banks">sixth largest bank in the world</a> by total assets,<sup id="cite_ref-SP_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SP-4">[4]</a></sup> with total assets of US$2.687 <a href="/wiki/10%5E12" class="mw-redirect" title="10^12">trillion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4Q19_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4Q19-5">[5]</a></sup> It is also the world's most valuable bank by <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> JPMorgan Chase is incorporated in Delaware.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn org">JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co.</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" Bank</a><br><a href="/wiki/J.P._Morgan_%26_Co." title="J.P. Morgan Cazenove</a><br><a href="/wiki/One_Equity_Partners" title="One Equity Partners">One Equity Partners</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Basel_III" title="Basel III">Capital ratio</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;">15.8% (2019)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jpmorganchase.com/">www<wbr></wbr>.jpmorganchase<wbr></wbr>.com/</a></span> <span class="penicon"><a href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q192314?uselang=en#P856" title="Edit this on Wikidata"><img alt="Edit this on Wikidata" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/10px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png" decoding="async" width="10" height="10" style="vertical-align: text-top" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/15px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8a/OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg/20px-OOjs_UI_icon_edit-ltr-progressive.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height: 1.35em;"><b>Footnotes / references</b><br><sup id="cite_ref-FY_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FY-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><p>As a "<a href="/wiki/Bulge_Bracket" title="Bulge Bracket">Bulge Bracket</a>" bank, it is a major provider of various investment banking and financial services. It is one of America's <a href="/wiki/Big_Four_(banking)#United_States" title="Big Four (banking)">Big Four banks</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">Bank of America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo" title="Wells Fargo">Wells Fargo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> JPMorgan Chase is considered to be a <a href="/wiki/Universal_bank" title="Universal bank">universal bank</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Custodian_bank" title="Custodian bank">custodian bank</a>. The J.P. Morgan brand, is used by the <a href="/wiki/Investment_banking" title="Investment banking">investment banking</a>, <a href="/wiki/J.P._Morgan_Asset_Management" class="mw-redirect" title="J.P. Morgan Asset Management">asset</a> <a href="/wiki/Asset_management" title="Asset management">management</a>, <a href="/wiki/Private_banking" title="Private banking">private banking</a>, private <a href="/wiki/Wealth_management" title="Wealth management">wealth management</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Treasury_services" title="Treasury services">treasury services</a> divisions. <a href="/wiki/Trust_law" title="Trust law">Fiduciary</a> activity within private banking and private wealth management is done under the aegis of JPMorgan Chase Bank, N.A.—the actual <a href="/wiki/Trustee" title="Trustee">trustee</a>. The Chase brand is used for <a href="/wiki/Credit_card" title="Credit card">credit card</a> services in the United States and Canada, the bank's <a href="/wiki/Retail_banking" title="Retail banking">retail banking</a> activities in the United States, and <a href="/wiki/Commercial_bank" title="Commercial bank">commercial banking</a>. Both the retail and commercial bank and the bank's <a href="/wiki/Corporate_headquarters" title="Corporate headquarters">corporate headquarters</a> are currently located at <a href="/wiki/383_Madison_Avenue" title="383 Madison Avenue">383 Madison Avenue</a> in <a href="/wiki/Midtown_Manhattan" title="Midtown Manhattan">Midtown Manhattan</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, while the prior headquarters building directly across the street, <a href="/wiki/270_Park_Avenue" title="270 Park Avenue">270 Park Avenue</a>, is demolished and replaced with a new building.<sup id="cite_ref-JPMH_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPMH-9">[9]</a></sup> The current company was originally known as Chemical Bank, which acquired Chase Manhattan and assumed that company's name. The present company was formed in 2000, when <a href="/wiki/Chase_Bank" title="Chase Bank">Chase Manhattan Corporation</a> merged with <a href="/wiki/J.P._Morgan_%26_Co." title="J.P. Morgan &amp; Co.">J.P. Morgan &amp; Co.</a><sup id="cite_ref-JPMH_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPMH-9">[9]</a></sup></p><p>As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the asset management arm of the bank has US$2.988 trillion in <a href="/wiki/Assets_under_management" title="Assets under management">assets under management</a>, while its investment and corporate bank arm holds US$25.45 trillion in <a href="/wiki/Custodian_bank" title="Custodian bank">assets under custody</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2Q19_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2Q19-10">[10]</a></sup> At US$45.0 billion in assets under management, the <a href="/wiki/Hedge_fund" title="Hedge fund">hedge fund</a> unit of JPMorgan Chase is the third largest hedge fund in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JPMorgan_Chase.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/JPMorgan_Chase.svg/220px-JPMorgan_Chase.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="25" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="170" data-file-height="19"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 25px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/JPMorgan_Chase.svg/220px-JPMorgan_Chase.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="25" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/JPMorgan_Chase.svg/330px-JPMorgan_Chase.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/JPMorgan_Chase.svg/440px-JPMorgan_Chase.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JPMorgan_Chase.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The JPMorgan Chase logo prior to the 2008 rebranding</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:J_P_Morgan_Logo_2008_1.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/J_P_Morgan_Logo_2008_1.svg/220px-J_P_Morgan_Logo_2008_1.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="47" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="98" data-file-height="21"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 47px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/J_P_Morgan_Logo_2008_1.svg/220px-J_P_Morgan_Logo_2008_1.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="47" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/J_P_Morgan_Logo_2008_1.svg/330px-J_P_Morgan_Logo_2008_1.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/J_P_Morgan_Logo_2008_1.svg/440px-J_P_Morgan_Logo_2008_1.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:J_P_Morgan_Logo_2008_1.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>As of June 2008, the JPMorgan logo used for the company's Investment Banking, Asset Management, and Treasury &amp; Securities Services units.<sup id="cite_ref-Robert_Cameron_TimesLogo_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robert_Cameron_TimesLogo-12">[12]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>JPMorgan Chase, in its current structure, is the result of the combination of several large U.S. banking companies since 1996, including <a href="/wiki/Chase_Manhattan_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Chase Manhattan Bank">Chase Manhattan Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/J.P._Morgan_%26_Co." title="J.P. Morgan &amp; Co.">J.P. Morgan &amp; Co.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bank_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank One">Bank One</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bear_Stearns" title="Bear Stearns">Bear Stearns</a> and <a href="/wiki/Washington_Mutual" title="Washington Mutual">Washington Mutual</a>. Going back further, its predecessors include major banking firms among which are <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Bank" title="Chemical Bank">Chemical Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manufacturers_Hanover" class="mw-redirect" title="Manufacturers Hanover">Manufacturers Hanover</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_Chicago_Bank" title="First Chicago Bank">First Chicago Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Detroit" title="National Bank of Detroit">National Bank of Detroit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas_Commerce_Bank" title="Texas Commerce Bank">Texas Commerce Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Providian_Financial" class="mw-redirect" title="Providian Financial">Providian Financial</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Western Bank">Great Western Bank</a>. The company's oldest predecessor institution, the <a href="/wiki/The_Manhattan_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="The Manhattan Company">Bank of the Manhattan Company</a>, was the third oldest banking corporation in the United States, and the 31st oldest bank in the world, having been established on September 1, 1799, by <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Burr" title="Aaron Burr">Aaron Burr</a>.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Chase_Manhattan_Bank">Chase Manhattan Bank</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Chase Manhattan Bank" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Chase_Manhattan_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Chase Manhattan Bank">Chase Manhattan Bank</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chase_logo_pre_historical.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2d/Chase_logo_pre_historical.jpg/220px-Chase_logo_pre_historical.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="218" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="227" data-file-height="225"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 218px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2d/Chase_logo_pre_historical.jpg/220px-Chase_logo_pre_historical.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="218" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chase_logo_pre_historical.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The logo used by Chase following the merger with the Manhattan Bank in 1954</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Chase_Manhattan_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Chase Manhattan Bank">Chase Manhattan Bank</a> was formed upon the 1955 purchase of <a href="/wiki/Chase_National_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Chase National Bank">Chase National Bank</a> (established in 1877) by the <a href="/wiki/The_Manhattan_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="The Manhattan Company">Bank of the Manhattan Company</a> (established in 1799),<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> the company's oldest predecessor institution. The Bank of the Manhattan Company was the creation of <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Burr" title="Aaron Burr">Aaron Burr</a>, who transformed The Manhattan Company from a water carrier into a bank.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p><p>According to page 115 of <i>An Empire of Wealth</i> by <a href="/wiki/John_Steele_Gordon" title="John Steele Gordon">John Steele Gordon</a>, the origin of this strand of JPMorgan Chase's history runs as follows:
</p>
<blockquote><p>At the turn of the nineteenth century, obtaining a bank charter required an act of the state legislature. This of course injected a powerful element of politics into the process and invited what today would be called corruption but then was regarded as business as usual. <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton" title="Alexander Hamilton">Hamilton</a>'s political enemy—and eventual murderer—<a href="/wiki/Aaron_Burr" title="Aaron Burr">Aaron Burr</a> was able to create a bank by sneaking a clause into a charter for a company, called the Manhattan Company, to provide clean water to New York City. The innocuous-looking clause allowed the company to invest surplus capital in any lawful enterprise. Within six months of the company's creation, and long before it had laid a single section of water pipe, the company opened a bank, the Bank of the Manhattan Company. Still in existence, it is today J. P. Morgan Chase, the largest bank in the United States.</p></blockquote>
<p>Led by <a href="/wiki/David_Rockefeller" title="David Rockefeller">David Rockefeller</a> during the 1970s and 1980s, Chase Manhattan emerged as one of the largest and most prestigious banking concerns, with leadership positions in syndicated lending, treasury and securities services, credit cards, mortgages, and retail financial services. Weakened by the real estate collapse in the early 1990s, it was acquired by <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Bank" title="Chemical Bank">Chemical Bank</a> in 1996, retaining the Chase name.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-16">[16]</a></sup> Before its merger with J.P. Morgan &amp; Co., the new Chase expanded the investment and asset management groups through two acquisitions. In 1999, it acquired San Francisco-based <a href="/wiki/Hambrecht_%26_Quist" title="Hambrecht &amp; Quist">Hambrecht &amp; Quist</a> for $1.35 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> In April 2000, UK-based <a href="/wiki/Robert_Fleming_%26_Co." title="Robert Fleming &amp; Co.">Robert Fleming &amp; Co.</a> was purchased by the new Chase Manhattan Bank for $7.7 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Chemical_Banking_Corporation">Chemical Banking Corporation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Chemical Banking Corporation" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Bank" title="Chemical Bank">Chemical Bank</a></div>
<p>The New York Chemical Manufacturing Company was founded in 1823 as a maker of various chemicals. In 1824, the company amended its <a href="/wiki/Charter" title="Charter">charter</a> to perform banking activities and created the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Bank_of_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Chemical Bank of New York">Chemical Bank of New York</a>. After 1851, the bank was separated from its parent and grew organically and through a series of mergers, most notably with <a href="/wiki/Corn_Exchange_Bank" title="Corn Exchange Bank">Corn Exchange Bank</a> in 1954, <a href="/wiki/Texas_Commerce_Bank" title="Texas Commerce Bank">Texas Commerce Bank</a> (a large bank in Texas) in 1986, and <a href="/wiki/Manufacturer%27s_Hanover_Trust_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Manufacturer's Hanover Trust Company">Manufacturer's Hanover Trust Company</a> in 1991 (the first major bank merger "among equals"). In the 1980s and early 1990s, Chemical emerged as one of the leaders in the financing of <a href="/wiki/Leveraged_buyout" title="Leveraged buyout">leveraged buyout</a> transactions. In 1984, Chemical launched <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Venture_Partners" class="mw-redirect" title="Chemical Venture Partners">Chemical Venture Partners</a> to invest in <a href="/wiki/Private_equity" title="Private equity">private equity</a> transactions alongside various <a href="/wiki/Financial_sponsor" title="Financial sponsor">financial sponsors</a>. By the late 1980s, Chemical developed its reputation for financing buyouts, building a <a href="/wiki/Leveraged_finance" class="mw-redirect" title="Leveraged finance">syndicated leveraged finance</a> business and related advisory businesses under the auspices of pioneering investment banker, <a href="/wiki/James_B._Lee,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="James B. Lee, Jr.">Jimmy Lee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> At many points throughout this history, Chemical Bank was the largest bank in the United States (either in terms of <a href="/wiki/Assets" class="mw-redirect" title="Assets">assets</a> or <a href="/wiki/Deposit_market_share" title="Deposit market share">deposit market share</a>).
</p><p>In 1996, Chemical Bank acquired Chase Manhattan. Although Chemical was the nominal survivor, it took the better-known Chase name.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-16">[16]</a></sup> To this day, JPMorgan Chase retains Chemical's pre-1996 stock price history, as well as Chemical's former headquarters site at <a href="/wiki/270_Park_Avenue" title="270 Park Avenue">270 Park Avenue</a> (with the current building being demolished for a replacement headquarters on the same site).
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="J.P._Morgan_.26_Company"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="J.P._Morgan_&amp;_Company">J.P. Morgan &amp; Company</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: J.P. Morgan &amp; Company" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/J.P._Morgan_%26_Co." title="J.P. Morgan &amp; Co.">J.P. Morgan &amp; Co.</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JP_Morgan_logo.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/JP_Morgan_logo.jpg/220px-JP_Morgan_logo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="52" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="430" data-file-height="102"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 52px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/JP_Morgan_logo.jpg/220px-JP_Morgan_logo.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="52" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JP_Morgan_logo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The J.P. Morgan &amp; Co. logo before its merger with Chase Manhattan Bank in 2000</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Banking_Influence_in_Large_Corporations,_1914.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Banking_Influence_in_Large_Corporations%2C_1914.jpg/220px-Banking_Influence_in_Large_Corporations%2C_1914.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3020" data-file-height="1830"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 133px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Banking_Influence_in_Large_Corporations%2C_1914.jpg/220px-Banking_Influence_in_Large_Corporations%2C_1914.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="133" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Banking_Influence_in_Large_Corporations,_1914.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Influence of J.P. Morgan in Large Corporations, 1914</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wallstreetbmb.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Wallstreetbmb.jpg/220px-Wallstreetbmb.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="683" data-file-height="545"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 176px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Wallstreetbmb.jpg/220px-Wallstreetbmb.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="176" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wallstreetbmb.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The J.P. Morgan headquarters in New York City following the September 16, 1920 bomb explosion that took the lives of 38 and injured over 400</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/House_of_Morgan" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Morgan">House of Morgan</a> was born out of the partnership of <a href="/wiki/Drexel,_Morgan_%26_Co." class="mw-redirect" title="Drexel, Morgan &amp; Co.">Drexel, Morgan &amp; Co.</a>, which in 1895 was renamed <a href="/wiki/J.P._Morgan_%26_Co." title="J.P. Morgan &amp; Co.">J.P. Morgan &amp; Co.</a> (see also: <a href="/wiki/J._Pierpont_Morgan" class="mw-redirect" title="J. Pierpont Morgan">J. Pierpont Morgan</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-:2_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-21">[21]</a></sup> J.P. Morgan &amp; Co. financed the formation of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Steel_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Steel Corporation">United States Steel Corporation</a>, which took over the business of <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">Andrew Carnegie</a> and others and was the world's first billion dollar corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> In 1895, J.P. Morgan &amp; Co. supplied the United States government with $62 million in gold to float a bond issue and restore the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Treasury" title="United States Department of the Treasury">treasury</a> surplus of $100 million.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In 1892, the company began to finance the <a href="/wiki/New_York,_New_Haven_and_Hartford_Railroad" title="New York, New Haven and Hartford Railroad">New York, New Haven and Hartford Railroad</a> and led it through a series of acquisitions that made it the dominant railroad transporter in New England.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p><p>Built in 1914, <a href="/wiki/23_Wall_Street" title="23 Wall Street">23 Wall Street</a> was the bank’s headquarters for decades. On September 16, 1920, a <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_bombing" title="Wall Street bombing">terrorist bomb exploded in front of the bank</a>, injuring 400 and killing 38.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Shortly before the bomb went off, a warning note was placed in a mailbox at the corner of Cedar Street and Broadway. The case has never been solved, and was rendered inactive by the FBI in 1940.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p><p>In August 1914, <a href="/wiki/Henry_P._Davison" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry P. Davison">Henry P. Davison</a>, a Morgan partner, made a deal with the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_England" title="Bank of England">Bank of England</a> to make J.P. Morgan &amp; Co. the monopoly underwriter of <a href="/wiki/War_bonds" class="mw-redirect" title="War bonds">war bonds</a> for the UK and France. The Bank of England became a "<a href="/wiki/Fiscal_agent" title="Fiscal agent">fiscal agent</a>" of J.P. Morgan &amp; Co., and vice versa.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-27">[27]</a></sup> The company also invested in the suppliers of <a href="/wiki/War_equipment" class="mw-redirect" title="War equipment">war equipment</a> to Britain and France. The company profited from the financing and purchasing activities of the two European governments.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-27">[27]</a></sup></p><p>In the 1930s, J.P. Morgan &amp; Co. and all integrated banking businesses in the United States were required by the provisions of the <a href="/wiki/Glass%E2%80%93Steagall_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Glass–Steagall Act">Glass–Steagall Act</a> to separate their <a href="/wiki/Investment_banking" title="Investment banking">investment banking</a> from their <a href="/wiki/Commercial_banking" class="mw-redirect" title="Commercial banking">commercial banking</a> operations. J.P. Morgan &amp; Co. chose to operate as a commercial bank.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (February 2020)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In 1935, after being barred from securities business for over a year, the heads of J.P. Morgan spun off its investment-banking operations. Led by J.P. Morgan partners, <a href="/wiki/Henry_S._Morgan" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry S. Morgan">Henry S. Morgan</a> (son of Jack Morgan and grandson of <a href="/wiki/J._Pierpont_Morgan" class="mw-redirect" title="J. Pierpont Morgan">J. Pierpont Morgan</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Harold_Stanley" title="Harold Stanley">Harold Stanley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">Morgan Stanley</a> was founded on September 16, 1935, with $6.6 million of nonvoting preferred stock from J.P. Morgan partners.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (February 2020)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In order to bolster its position, in 1959, J.P. Morgan merged with the Guaranty Trust Company of New York to form the Morgan Guaranty Trust Company.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-21">[21]</a></sup> The bank would continue to operate as Morgan Guaranty Trust until the 1980s, before migrating back to the use of the J.P. Morgan brand. In 1984, the group purchased the Purdue National Corporation of Lafayette Indiana. In 1988, the company once again began operating exclusively as J.P. Morgan &amp; Co.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Bank_One_Corporation">Bank One Corporation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Bank One Corporation" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bank_One_Corporation" title="Bank One Corporation">Bank One Corporation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:176px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bank_One_logo.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ae/Bank_One_logo.png" decoding="async" width="174" height="32" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="174" data-file-height="32"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 174px;height: 32px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ae/Bank_One_logo.png" data-alt="" data-width="174" data-height="32" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bank_One_logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logo of Bank One</div></div></div>
<p>In 2004, JPMorgan Chase merged with Chicago-based <a href="/wiki/Bank_One_Corporation" title="Bank One Corporation">Bank One Corp.</a>, bringing on board current Chairman and CEO <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Dimon" title="Jamie Dimon">Jamie Dimon</a> as president and COO.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> He succeeded former CEO <a href="/wiki/William_B._Harrison,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="William B. Harrison, Jr.">William B. Harrison, Jr.</a><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Dimon introduced new cost-cutting strategies, and replaced former JPMorgan Chase executives in key positions with Bank One executives—many of whom were with Dimon at <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a>. Dimon became CEO in December 2005 and Chairman in December 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Bank_One_Corporation" title="Bank One Corporation">Bank One Corporation</a> was formed with the 1998 merger of Banc One of <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus, Ohio</a> and <a href="/wiki/First_Chicago_Bank" title="First Chicago Bank">First Chicago NBD</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> This merger was  considered a failure until Dimon took over and reformed the new firm's practices. Dimon effected changes to make Bank One Corporation a viable merger partner for JPMorgan Chase.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:First_Chicago_Bank_Logo.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3f/First_Chicago_Bank_Logo.png/220px-First_Chicago_Bank_Logo.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="36" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="446" data-file-height="73"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 36px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3f/First_Chicago_Bank_Logo.png/220px-First_Chicago_Bank_Logo.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="36" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:First_Chicago_Bank_Logo.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The First Chicago Bank logo</div></div></div>
<p>Bank One Corporation, formerly First Bancgroup of Ohio, was founded as a holding company for City National Bank of Columbus, Ohio and several other banks in that state, all of which were renamed "Bank One" when the holding company was renamed Banc One Corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> With the beginning of interstate banking they spread into other states, always renaming acquired banks "Bank One." After the <a href="/wiki/First_Chicago_Bank" title="First Chicago Bank">First Chicago NBD</a> merger, adverse financial results led to the departure of CEO <a href="/wiki/John_B._McCoy" title="John B. McCoy">John B. McCoy</a>, whose father and grandfather had headed Banc One and predecessors. JPMorgan Chase completed the acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Bank_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank One">Bank One</a> in the third quarter of 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Bear_Stearns">Bear Stearns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Bear Stearns" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bear_Stearns" title="Bear Stearns">Bear Stearns</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bear_Stearns_Logo.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bear_Stearns_Logo.svg/220px-Bear_Stearns_Logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="98" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="193" data-file-height="86"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 98px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bear_Stearns_Logo.svg/220px-Bear_Stearns_Logo.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="98" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bear_Stearns_Logo.svg/330px-Bear_Stearns_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Bear_Stearns_Logo.svg/440px-Bear_Stearns_Logo.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bear_Stearns_Logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Bear Stearns logo</div></div></div>
<p>At the end of 2007, <a href="/wiki/Bear_Stearns" title="Bear Stearns">Bear Stearns</a> was the fifth largest investment bank in the United States but its market capitalization had deteriorated through the second half of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-38">[38]</a></sup> On Friday, March 14, 2008, Bear Stearns lost 47% of its equity market value as rumors emerged that clients were withdrawing capital from the bank. Over the following weekend, it emerged that Bear Stearns might prove <a href="/wiki/Insolvent" class="mw-redirect" title="Insolvent">insolvent</a>, and on March 15, 2008, the Federal Reserve engineered a deal to prevent a wider systemic crisis from the collapse of Bear Stearns.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-39">[39]</a></sup></p><p>On March 16, 2008, after a weekend of intense negotiations between JPMorgan, Bear, and the federal government, JPMorgan Chase announced its plans to acquire Bear Stearns in a <a href="/wiki/Stock_swap" title="Stock swap">stock swap</a> worth $2.00 per share or $240 million pending shareholder approval scheduled within 90 days.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-39">[39]</a></sup> In the interim, JPMorgan Chase agreed to guarantee all Bear Stearns trades and business process flows.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> On March 18, 2008, JPMorgan Chase formally announced the acquisition of Bear Stearns for $236 million.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-38">[38]</a></sup> The stock swap agreement was signed that night.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p><p>On March 24, 2008, after public discontent over the low acquisition price threatened the deal's closure, a revised offer was announced at approximately $10 per share.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-38">[38]</a></sup> Under the revised terms, JPMorgan also immediately acquired a 39.5% stake in Bear Stearns using newly issued shares at the new offer price and gained a commitment from the board, representing another 10% of the share capital, that its members would vote in favor of the new deal. With sufficient commitments to ensure a successful shareholder vote, the merger was completed on May 30, 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Washington_Mutual">Washington Mutual</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Washington Mutual" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Washington_Mutual" title="Washington Mutual">Washington Mutual</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wamu.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Wamu.svg/220px-Wamu.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="68" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="124"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 68px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Wamu.svg/220px-Wamu.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="68" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Wamu.svg/330px-Wamu.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Wamu.svg/440px-Wamu.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wamu.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Washington Mutual logo prior to its 2008 acquisition by JPMorgan Chase</div></div></div>
<p>On September 25, 2008, JPMorgan Chase bought most of the banking operations of <a href="/wiki/Washington_Mutual" title="Washington Mutual">Washington Mutual</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Receivership" title="Receivership">receivership</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Deposit_Insurance_Corporation" title="Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation">Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation</a>. That night, the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Thrift_Supervision" title="Office of Thrift Supervision">Office of Thrift Supervision</a>, in what was by far the largest bank failure in American history, had seized Washington Mutual Bank and placed it into receivership. The FDIC sold the bank's assets, secured debt obligations and deposits to JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co for $1.836 billion, which re-opened the bank the following day. As a result of the takeover, Washington Mutual shareholders lost all their <a href="/wiki/Equity_investment" class="mw-redirect" title="Equity investment">equity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p><p>JPMorgan Chase raised $10 billion in a stock sale to cover writedowns and losses after taking on deposits and branches of Washington Mutual.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> Through the acquisition, JPMorgan now owns the former accounts of <a href="/wiki/Providian_Financial" class="mw-redirect" title="Providian Financial">Providian Financial</a>, a credit card issuer WaMu acquired in 2005. The company announced plans to complete the rebranding of Washington Mutual branches to Chase by late 2009.
</p><p>Chief executive <a href="/wiki/Alan_H._Fishman" title="Alan H. Fishman">Alan H. Fishman</a> received a $7.5 million sign-on bonus and cash severance of $11.6 million after being CEO for 17 days.<sup id="cite_ref-payout_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-payout-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_settlement">2013 settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2013 settlement" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On November 19, 2013, the Justice Department announced that JPMorgan Chase agreed to pay $13 billion to settle investigations into its business practices pertaining to mortgage-backed securities.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Of that amount, $9 billion was penalties and fines and the remaining $4 billion was consumer relief. This was the largest corporate settlement to date. Conduct at Bear Stearns and Washington Mutual prior to their 2008 acquisitions accounted for much of the alleged wrongdoing. The agreement did not settle criminal charges.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_recent_acquisitions">Other recent acquisitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Other recent acquisitions" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2006, JPMorgan Chase purchased <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_Funding_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Collegiate Funding Services">Collegiate Funding Services</a>, a portfolio company of private equity firm <a href="/wiki/Lightyear_Capital" title="Lightyear Capital">Lightyear Capital</a>, for $663 million. CFS was used as the foundation for the Chase Student Loans, previously known as Chase Education Finance.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2006, JPMorgan Chase acquired <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_New_York_Mellon" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of New York Mellon">Bank of New York Mellon</a>'s retail and small business banking network. The acquisition gave Chase access to 339 additional branches in New York, New Jersey, and Connecticut.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2008, JPMorgan acquired the UK-based <a href="/wiki/Carbon_offset" title="Carbon offset">carbon offsetting</a> company <a href="/wiki/Climate_Care" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate Care">ClimateCare</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p><p>In November 2009, JPMorgan announced it would acquire the balance of JPMorgan Cazenove, an advisory and underwriting joint venture established in 2004 with the <a href="/wiki/Cazenove_(stock_broker)" title="Cazenove (stock broker)">Cazenove Group</a>, for GBP1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2013, JPMorgan acquired Bloomspot, a San Francisco-based startup in the "deals" space for $35 million. Shortly after the acquisition, the service was shut down and Bloomspot's talent was left unused.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisition_history">Acquisition history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Acquisition history" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>

</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr><td class="clade-slabel last" style="border-right:none;border-left:none;"> 
</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Recent history" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In October 2014, JPMorgan sold its commodities trader unit to Mercuria for $800 million, a quarter of the initial valuation of $3.5 billion, as the transaction excluded some oil and metal stockpiles and other assets.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2016, JPMorgan decided not to finance <a href="/wiki/Coal_mine" class="mw-redirect" title="Coal mine">coal mines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coal_power_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Coal power plant">coal power plants</a> in wealthy countries.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> In September 2016, JPMorgan made an equity investment in InvestCloud.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> In December 2016, 14 former executives of the Wendel investment company faced trial for tax fraud while JP Morgan Chase was to be pursued for complicity. Jean-Bernard Lafonta was convicted last December<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (August 2017)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> for spreading false information and insider trading, and fined 1.5 million euros.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2017, Lawrence Obracanik, a former JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co employee, pleaded guilty to criminal charges that he stole more than $5 million from his employer to pay personal debts.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> In June 2017, Matt Zames, the now former COO of the bank decided to leave the firm.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> In December 2017, JP Morgan was sued by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_Nigeria" title="Federal government of Nigeria">Nigerian government</a> for $875 million, which <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> alleges was transferred by JP Morgan to a corrupt former minister.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Nigeria accused JP Morgan of being "grossly negligent".<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2018, <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> reported that JP Morgan "agreed to pay $5.3 million to settle allegations it violated <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Assets_Control_Regulations" title="Cuban Assets Control Regulations">Cuban Assets Control Regulations</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_sanctions_against_Iran" title="United States sanctions against Iran">Iranian sanctions</a> and Weapons of Mass Destruction sanctions 87 times, the U.S. Treasury said".<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2019, JP Morgan announced the launch of <a href="/wiki/JPM_Coin" title="JPM Coin">JPM Coin</a>, a digital token that will be used to settle transactions between clients of its wholesale payments business.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> It is the first cryptocurrency issued by a United States bank.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_data">Financial data</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Financial data" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
