</p><p>JPMorgan Chase<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> was the biggest bank at the end of 2008 as an individual bank (not including subsidiaries). As of 2019, JPMorgan Chase is ranked #18 on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> rankings of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="CEO-to-worker_pay_ratio">CEO-to-worker pay ratio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: CEO-to-worker pay ratio" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>For the first time in 2018, a new Securities and Exchange Commission rule mandated under the 2010 Dodd-Frank financial reform requires publicly traded companies to disclose how their CEOs are compensated in comparison with their employees. In public filings, companies have to disclose their "Pay Ratios," or the CEO's compensation divided by the median employee's.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2017">2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2017" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>According to SEC filings, JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co. paid its CEO $28,320,175 in 2017. The average worker employed by JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co. was paid $77,799 in 2017; thus marking a CEO-to-worker Pay Ratio of 364 to 1.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> As of April 2018, steelmaker Nucor represented the median CEO-to-worker Pay Ratio from SEC filings with values of 133 to 1.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> <i>Bloomberg BusinessWeek</i> on May 2, 2013 found the ratio of CEO pay to the typical worker rose from about 20-to-1 in the 1950s to 120-to-1 in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2018">2018</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 2018" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Total 2018 compensation for <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Dimon" title="Jamie Dimon">Jamie Dimon</a>, CEO, was $30,040,153, and total compensation of the median employee was determined to be $78,923. The resulting pay ratio was estimated to be 381:1.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Structure" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<p>JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co. owns five bank subsidiaries in the United States:<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chase_(bank)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chase (bank)">JPMorgan Chase Bank, National Association</a>; Chase Bank USA, National Association; Custodial Trust Company; JPMorgan Chase Bank, Dearborn; and J.P. Morgan Bank and Trust Company, National Association.
</p><p>For management reporting purposes, JPMorgan Chase's activities are organized into a corporate/private equity segment and four business segments; consumer and community banking, corporate and investment bank, commercial banking, and asset management.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The investment banking division at J.P. Morgan is divided by teams: industry, M&amp;A and capital markets. Industry teams include consumer and retail, healthcare, diversified industries and transportation, natural resources, financial institutions, metals and mining, real estate and technology, media and telecommunications.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="JPMorgan_Europe.2C_Ltd."></span><span class="mw-headline" id="JPMorgan_Europe,_Ltd.">JPMorgan Europe, Ltd.</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: JPMorgan Europe, Ltd." data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/J.P._Morgan_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="J.P. Morgan in the United Kingdom">J.P. Morgan in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<p>The company, known previously as Chase Manhattan International Limited, was founded on September 18, 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2008, the bank announced plans to construct a new European headquarters at <a href="/wiki/Riverside_South_(Canary_Wharf)" title="Riverside South (Canary Wharf)">Canary Wharf</a>, London.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> These plans were subsequently suspended in December 2010, when the bank announced the purchase of a nearby existing office tower at <a href="/wiki/25_Bank_Street" title="25 Bank Street">25 Bank Street</a> for use as the European headquarters of its investment bank.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> 25 Bank Street had originally been designated as the European headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Enron" title="Enron">Enron</a> and was subsequently used as the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Lehman_Brothers" title="Lehman Brothers">Lehman Brothers International (Europe)</a>.
</p><p>The regional office is in London with offices in <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth" title="Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> for <a href="/wiki/Asset_management" title="Asset management">asset management</a>, private banking, and investment.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Operations" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<p>Earlier in 2011, the company announced that by the use of supercomputers, the time taken to assess risk had been greatly reduced, from arriving at a conclusion within hours to what is now minutes. The banking corporation uses for this calculation <a href="/wiki/Field-programmable_gate_array" title="Field-programmable gate array">Field-Programmable Gate Array technology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: History" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The Bank began operations in Japan in 1924,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> in Australia during the later part of the nineteenth century,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> and in Indonesia during the early 1920s.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> An office of the Equitable Eastern Banking Corporation (one of J.P. Morgan's predecessors) opened a branch in China in 1921 and Chase National Bank was established there in 1923.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> The bank has operated in Saudi Arabia<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> and India<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> since the 1930s. Chase Manhattan Bank opened an office in Korea in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> The firm's presence in Greece dates to 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-ceemea_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ceemea-103">[103]</a></sup> An office of JPMorgan was opened in Taiwan in 1970,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> in Russia (Soviet Union) in 1973,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic</a> operations began during the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Operations in Poland began in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-ceemea_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ceemea-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Lobbying">Lobbying</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Lobbying" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<p>JP Morgan Chase's PAC and its employees contributed $2.6 million to federal campaigns in 2014 and financed its lobbying team with $4.7 million in the first three quarters of 2014. JP Morgan's giving has been focused on Republicans, with 62 percent of its donations going to GOP recipients in 2014. Still, 78 House Democrats received campaign cash from JPMorgan's PAC in the 2014 cycle at an average of $5,200 and a total of 38 of the Democrats who voted for the 2015 spending bill took money from JPMorgan's PAC in 2014. JP Morgan Chase's PAC made maximum donations to the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Congressional_Campaign_Committee" title="Democratic Congressional Campaign Committee">Democratic Congressional Campaign Committee</a> and the leadership PACs of <a href="/wiki/Steny_Hoyer" title="Steny Hoyer">Steny Hoyer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jim_Himes" title="Jim Himes">Jim Himes</a> in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-crp_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crp-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Controversies" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Conflicts_of_interest_on_investment_research">Conflicts of interest on investment research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Conflicts of interest on investment research" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In December 2002, Chase paid fines totaling $80 million, with the amount split between the states and the federal government. The fines were part of a settlement involving charges that ten banks, including Chase, deceived investors with biased research. The total settlement with the ten banks was $1.4 billion. The settlement required that the banks separate investment banking from research, and ban any allocation of IPO shares.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Enron">Enron</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Enron" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Enron_scandal" title="Enron scandal">Enron scandal</a></div>
<p>Chase paid out over $2 billion in fines and legal settlements for their role in financing <a href="/wiki/Enron" title="Enron">Enron</a> Corporation with aiding and abetting Enron Corp.'s securities fraud, which collapsed amid a financial scandal in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> In 2003, Chase paid $160 million in fines and penalties to settle claims by the Securities and Exchange Commission and the Manhattan district attorney's office. In 2005, Chase paid $2.2 billion to settle a lawsuit filed by investors in Enron.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="WorldCom">WorldCom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: WorldCom" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>JPMorgan Chase, which helped <a href="/wiki/Underwrite" class="mw-redirect" title="Underwrite">underwrite</a> $15.4 billion of <a href="/wiki/WorldCom" class="mw-redirect" title="WorldCom">WorldCom</a>'s bonds, agreed in March 2005 to pay $2 billion; that was 46 percent, or $630 million, more than it would have paid had it accepted an investor offer in May 2004 of $1.37 billion. J.P. Morgan was the last big lender to settle. Its payment is the second largest in the case, exceeded only by the $2.6 billion accord reached in 2004 by <a href="/wiki/Citigroup" title="Citigroup">Citigroup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> In March 2005, 16 of <a href="/wiki/WorldCom" class="mw-redirect" title="WorldCom">WorldCom</a>'s 17 former underwriters reached settlements with the investors.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Jefferson_County.2C_Alabama"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Jefferson_County,_Alabama">Jefferson County, Alabama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Jefferson County, Alabama" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In November 2009, a week after <a href="/wiki/Birmingham,_Alabama" title="Birmingham, Alabama">Birmingham, Alabama</a> Mayor <a href="/wiki/Larry_Langford" title="Larry Langford">Larry Langford</a> was convicted for financial crimes related to bond swaps for <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_Alabama" title="Jefferson County, Alabama">Jefferson County, Alabama</a>, JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co. agreed to a $722 million settlement with the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission</a> to end a probe into the sales of <a href="/wiki/Derivative_(finance)" title="Derivative (finance)">derivatives</a> that allegedly contributed to the near-bankruptcy of the county. JPMorgan had been chosen by the county commissioners to refinance the county's sewer debt, and the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">SEC</a> had alleged that JPMorgan made undisclosed payments to close friends of the commissioners in exchange for the deal and made up for the costs by charging higher interest rates on the swaps.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Failure_to_comply_with_client_money_rules_in_the_UK">Failure to comply with client money rules in the UK</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Failure to comply with client money rules in the UK" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In June 2010, J.P. Morgan Securities was fined a record <a href="/wiki/Pounds_sterling" class="mw-redirect" title="Pounds sterling">£</a>33.32 million ($49.12 million) by the UK <a href="/wiki/Financial_Services_Authority" title="Financial Services Authority">Financial Services Authority</a> (FSA) for failing to protect an average of £5.5 billion of clients' money from 2002 to 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AFXnews_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFXnews-116">[116]</a></sup> 
FSA requires financial firms to keep clients' funds in separate accounts to protect the clients in case such firm becomes insolvent. The firm had failed to properly segregate client funds from corporate funds following the merger of Chase and J.P. Morgan, resulting in a violation of FSA regulations but no losses to clients. The clients' funds would have been at risk had the firm become insolvent during this period.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> J.P. Morgan Securities reported the incident to the FSA, corrected the errors, and cooperated in the ensuing investigation, resulting in the fine being reduced 30% from an original amount of £47.6 million.<sup id="cite_ref-AFXnews_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFXnews-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Mortgage_overcharge_of_active_military_personnel">Mortgage overcharge of active military personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Mortgage overcharge of active military personnel" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In January 2011, JPMorgan Chase admitted that it wrongly overcharged several thousand military families for their mortgages, including active duty personnel in Afghanistan. The bank also admitted it improperly foreclosed on more than a dozen military families; both actions were in clear violation of the <a href="/wiki/Servicemembers_Civil_Relief_Act" title="Servicemembers Civil Relief Act">Servicemembers Civil Relief Act</a> which automatically lowers mortgage rates to 6 percent, and bars foreclosure proceedings of active duty personnel. The overcharges may have never come to light were it not for legal action taken by Captain Jonathan Rowles. Both Captain Rowles and his spouse Julia accused Chase of violating the law and harassing the couple for nonpayment. An official stated that the situation was "grim" and Chase initially stated it would be refunding up to $2,000,000 to those who were overcharged, and that families improperly foreclosed on have gotten or will get their homes back.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Chase has acknowledged that as many as 6,000 active duty military personnel were illegally overcharged, and more than 18 military families homes were wrongly foreclosed. In April, Chase agreed to pay a total of $27 million in compensation to settle the class-action suit.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> At the company's 2011 shareholders' meeting, Dimon apologized for the error and said the bank would forgive the loans of any active-duty personnel whose property had been foreclosed. In June 2011, lending chief Dave Lowman was forced out over the scandal.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Truth_in_Lending_Act_litigation">Truth in Lending Act litigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Truth in Lending Act litigation" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2008 and 2009, 14 lawsuits were filed against JPMorgan Chase in various district courts on behalf of Chase credit card holders claiming the bank violated the <a href="/wiki/Truth_in_Lending_Act" title="Truth in Lending Act">Truth in Lending Act</a>, breached its contract with the consumers and committed a breach of implied covenant of good faith and fair dealing. The consumers contended that Chase, with little or no notice, increased minimum monthly payments from 2% to 5% on loan balances that were transferred to consumers' credit cards based on the promise of a fixed interest rate. In May 2011, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Northern_District_of_California" title="United States District Court for the Northern District of California">United States District Court for the Northern District of California</a> certified the class action lawsuit. On July 23, 2012, Chase agreed to pay $100 million to settle the claim.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Alleged_manipulation_of_energy_market">Alleged manipulation of energy market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Alleged manipulation of energy market" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In July 2013, The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Energy_Regulatory_Commission" title="Federal Energy Regulatory Commission">Federal Energy Regulatory Commission</a> (FERC) approved a stipulation and consent agreement under which JPMorgan Ventures Energy Corporation (JPMVEC), a subsidiary of JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co., agreed to pay $410 million in penalties and <a href="/wiki/Disgorgement_(law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Disgorgement (law)">disgorgement</a> to ratepayers for allegations of <a href="/wiki/Market_manipulation" title="Market manipulation">market manipulation</a> stemming from the company's bidding activities in electricity markets in California and the Midwest from September 2010 through November 2012. JPMVEC agreed to pay a civil penalty of $285 million to the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Treasury" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Treasury">U.S. Treasury</a> and to disgorge $125 million in unjust profits. JPMVEC admitted the facts set forth in the agreement, but neither admitted nor denied the violations.<sup id="cite_ref-ferc-2013_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ferc-2013-123">[123]</a></sup></p><p>The case stemmed from multiple referrals to FERC from market monitors in 2011 and 2012 regarding JPMVEC's bidding practices. FERC investigators determined that JPMVEC engaged in 12 manipulative bidding strategies designed to make profits from power plants that were usually out of the money in the marketplace. In each of them, the company made bids designed to create artificial conditions that forced California and Midcontinent Independent System Operators (ISOs) to pay JPMVEC outside the market at premium rates.<sup id="cite_ref-ferc-2013_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ferc-2013-123">[123]</a></sup></p><p>FERC investigators further determined that JPMVEC knew that the California ISO and Midcontinent ISO received no benefit from making inflated payments to the company, thereby defrauding the ISOs by obtaining payments for benefits that the company did not deliver beyond the routine provision of energy. FERC investigators also determined that JPMVEC's bids displaced other generation and altered day ahead and real-time prices from the prices that would have resulted had the company not submitted the bids.<sup id="cite_ref-ferc-2013_123-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ferc-2013-123">[123]</a></sup></p><p>Under the <a href="/wiki/Energy_Policy_Act_of_2005" title="Energy Policy Act of 2005">Energy Policy Act of 2005</a>, Congress directed FERC to detect, prevent and appropriately sanction the gaming of energy markets. According to FERC, the Commission approved the settlement as in the public interest.<sup id="cite_ref-ferc-2013_123-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ferc-2013-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Criminal_investigation_into_obstruction_of_justice">Criminal investigation into obstruction of justice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Criminal investigation into obstruction of justice" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>FERC's investigation of energy market manipulations led to a subsequent investigation into possible obstruction of justice by employees of JPMorgan Chase.<sup id="cite_ref-flitter-2013_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flitter-2013-124">[124]</a></sup> Various newspapers reported in September 2013 that the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">Federal Bureau of Investigation</a> (FBI) and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Attorney_for_the_Southern_District_of_New_York" title="United States Attorney for the Southern District of New York">US Attorney's Office in Manhattan</a> were investigating whether employees withheld information or made false statements during the FERC investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-flitter-2013_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flitter-2013-124">[124]</a></sup> The reported impetus for the investigation was a letter from Massachusetts Senators <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Warren" title="Elizabeth Warren">Elizabeth Warren</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edward_Markey" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward Markey">Edward Markey</a>, in which they asked FERC why no action was taken against people who impeded the FERC investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-flitter-2013_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flitter-2013-124">[124]</a></sup> At the time of the FBI investigation, the Senate Permanent Subcommittee on Investigations was also looking into whether JPMorgan Chase employees impeded the FERC investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-flitter-2013_124-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flitter-2013-124">[124]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> reported that JPMorgan Chase was facing over a dozen investigations at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-flitter-2013_124-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flitter-2013-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Sanctions_violations">Sanctions violations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sanctions violations" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On August 25, 2011, JPMorgan Chase agreed to settle fines with regard to violations of the sanctions under the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Foreign_Assets_Control" title="Office of Foreign Assets Control">Office of Foreign Assets Control</a> (OFAC) regime. The U.S. Department of Treasury released the following civil penalties information under the heading: "JPMorgan Chase Bank N.A. Settles Apparent Violations of Multiple Sanctions Programs":
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>JPMorgan Chase Bank, N.A, New York, NY ("JPMC") has agreed to remit $88,300,000 to settle potential civil liability for apparent violations of: the Cuban Assets Control Regulations ("CACR"), 31 C.F.R. part 515; the Weapons of Mass Destruction Proliferators Sanctions Regulations ("WMDPSR"), 31 C.F.R. part 544; Executive Order 13382, "Blocking Property of Weapons of Mass Destruction Proliferators and Their Supporters;" the Global Terrorism Sanctions Regulations ("GTSR"), 31 C.F.R. part 594; the Iranian Transactions Regulations ("ITR"), 31 C.F.R. part 560; the Sudanese Sanctions Regulations ("SSR"), 31 C.F.R. part 538; the Former Liberian Regime of Charles Taylor Sanctions Regulations ("FLRCTSR"), 31 C.F.R. part 593; and the Reporting, Procedures, and Penalties Regulations ("RPPR"), 31 C.F.R. part 501, that occurred between December 15, 2005, and March 1, 2011.</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite>U.S. Department of the Treasury Resource Center, OFAC Recent Actions. Retrieved June 18, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Mortgage_Settlement">National Mortgage Settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: National Mortgage Settlement" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On February 9, 2012, it was announced that the five largest mortgage servicers (Ally/GMAC, Bank of America, Citi, JPMorgan Chase, and Wells Fargo) agreed to a historic settlement with the federal government and 49 states.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> The settlement, known as the National Mortgage Settlement (NMS), required the servicers to provide about $26 billion in relief to distressed homeowners and in direct payments to the states and federal government. This settlement amount makes the NMS the second largest civil settlement in U.S. history, only trailing the <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_Master_Settlement_Agreement" title="Tobacco Master Settlement Agreement">Tobacco Master Settlement Agreement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> The five banks were also required to comply with 305 new mortgage servicing standards. Oklahoma held out and agreed to settle with the banks separately.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Speculative_trading">Speculative trading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Speculative trading" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2012_JPMorgan_Chase_trading_loss" title="2012 JPMorgan Chase trading loss">2012 JPMorgan Chase trading loss</a></div>
<p>In 2012, JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co was charged for misrepresenting and failing to disclose that the CIO had engaged in extremely risky and speculative trades that exposed JPMorgan to significant losses.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Mortgage-backed_securities_sales">Mortgage-backed securities sales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Mortgage-backed securities sales" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In August 2013, JPMorgan Chase announced that it was being investigated by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">United States Department of Justice</a> over its offerings of <a href="/wiki/Mortgage-backed_security" title="Mortgage-backed security">mortgage-backed securities</a> leading up to the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" title="Financial crisis of 2007–08">financial crisis of 2007–08</a>. The company said that the Department of Justice had preliminarily concluded that the firm violated federal securities laws in offerings of <a href="/wiki/Subprime" class="mw-redirect" title="Subprime">subprime</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alt-A" title="Alt-A">Alt-A</a> residential mortgage securities during the period 2005 to 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id=".22Sons_and_Daughters.22_hiring_program"></span><span class="mw-headline" id='"Sons_and_Daughters"_hiring_program'>"Sons and Daughters" hiring program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title='Edit section: "Sons and Daughters" hiring program' data-section="35" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In November 2016, JPMorgan Chase agreed to pay $264 million in fines to settle civil and criminal charges involving a systematic bribery scheme spanning 2006 to 2013 in which the bank secured business deals in Hong Kong by agreeing to hire hundreds of friends and relatives of Chinese government officials, resulting in more than $100 million in revenue for the bank.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Madoff_fraud">Madoff fraud</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Madoff fraud" data-section="36" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Madoff_investment_scandal" title="Madoff investment scandal">Madoff investment scandal</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bernie_Madoff" title="Bernie Madoff">Bernie Madoff</a> opened a business account at Chemical Bank in 1986 and maintained it until 2008, long after Chemical acquired Chase.
</p><p>In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Irving_Picard" title="Irving Picard">Irving Picard</a>, the SIPC receiver appointed to liquidate Madoff's company, alleged that JPMorgan failed to prevent Madoff from defrauding his customers. According to the suit, Chase "knew or should have known" that Madoff's wealth management business was a fraud. However, Chase did not report its concerns to regulators or law enforcement until October 2008, when it notified the UK <a href="/wiki/Serious_Organised_Crime_Agency" title="Serious Organised Crime Agency">Serious Organised Crime Agency</a>. Picard argued that even after Morgan investment bankers reported its concerns about Madoff's performance to UK officials, Chase's retail banking division did not put any restrictions on Madoff's banking activities until his arrest two months later.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> The receiver's suit against J.P. Morgan was dismissed by the Court for failing to set forth any legally cognizable claim for damages.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p><p>In the fall of 2013, JPMorgan began talks with prosecutors and regulators regarding compliance with anti-money-laundering and know-your-customer banking regulations in connection with Madoff.
</p><p>On January 7, 2014, JPMorgan agreed to pay a total of $2.05 billion in fines and penalties to settle civil and criminal charges related to its role in the Madoff scandal. The government filed a two-count <a href="/wiki/Criminal_information" class="mw-redirect" title="Criminal information">criminal information</a> charging JPMorgan with Bank Secrecy Act violations, but the charges will be dismissed within two years provided that JPMorgan reforms its anti-money laundering procedures and cooperates with the government in its investigation. The bank agreed to forfeit $1.7 billion.
</p><p>The lawsuit, which was filed on behalf of shareholders against Chief Executive <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Dimon" title="Jamie Dimon">Jamie Dimon</a> and other high-ranking JPMorgan employees, used statements made by <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Madoff" title="Bernie Madoff">Bernie Madoff</a> during interviews conducted while in prison in <a href="/wiki/Butner,_North_Carolina" title="Butner, North Carolina">Butner, North Carolina</a> claiming that JPMorgan officials knew of the fraud. The lawsuit stated that, "JPMorgan was uniquely positioned for 20 years to see Madoff's crimes and put a stop to them ... But faced with the prospect of shutting down Madoff's account and losing lucrative profits, JPMorgan - at its highest level - chose to turn a blind eye."<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p><p>JPMorgan also agreed to pay a $350 million fine to the Office of the Comptroller of the Currency and settle the suit filed against it by Picard for $543 million.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption_investigation_in_Asia">Corruption investigation in Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Corruption investigation in Asia" data-section="37" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On March 26, 2014, the Hong Kong <a href="/wiki/Independent_Commission_Against_Corruption_(Hong_Kong)" title="Independent Commission Against Corruption (Hong Kong)">Independent Commission Against Corruption</a> seized computer records and documents after searching the office of Fang Fang, the company's outgoing chief executive officer for China investment banking.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="September_2014_cyber-attack">September 2014 cyber-attack</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: September 2014 cyber-attack" data-section="38" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2014_JPMorgan_Chase_data_breach" title="2014 JPMorgan Chase data breach">2014 JPMorgan Chase data breach</a></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Cyber-attack" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyber-attack">cyber-attack</a>, disclosed in September 2014, compromised the JPMorgan Chase accounts of over 83 million customers. The attack was discovered by the bank's security team in late July 2014, but not completely halted until the middle of August.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Alleged_discrimination_lawsuit">Alleged discrimination lawsuit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Alleged discrimination lawsuit" data-section="39" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In January 2017, the United States sued the company, accusing it of discriminating against "thousands" of black and <a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a> mortgage borrowers between 2006 and at least 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Improper_handling_of_ADRs">Improper handling of ADRs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Improper handling of ADRs" data-section="40" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On 26 December 2018, as part of an investigation by the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission</a> (SEC) into abusive practices related to <a href="/wiki/American_depositary_receipt" title="American depositary receipt">American depositary receipts</a> (ADRs), JPMorgan agreed to pay more than $135 million to settle charges of improper handling of "pre-released" ADRs without admitting or denying the SEC's findings. The sum consisted of $71 million in ill-gotten gains plus $14.4 million in prejudgment interest and an additional penalty of $49.7 million.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Investments_in_coal.2C_oil_and_gas_projects"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Investments_in_coal,_oil_and_gas_projects">Investments in coal, oil and gas projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Investments in coal, oil and gas projects" data-section="41" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>JPMorgan has come under criticism for investing in new coal, oil and gas projects since the Paris climate change agreement. From 2016 to the first half of 2019 it provided $75 billion (£61 billion) to companies expanding in sectors such as fracking and Arctic oil and gas exploration.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> According to Rainforest Action Network its total fossil fuel financing was $64 billion in 2018, $69 billion in 2017 and $62 billion in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Leaked_study_on_climate_change_impacts">Leaked study on climate change impacts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Leaked study on climate change impacts" data-section="42" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>An internal study, 'Risky business: the climate and macroeconomy', by bank economists David Mackie and Jessica Murray was leaked in early‑2020.  The report, dated 14<span class="nowrap"> </span>January 2020, states that under our current unsustainable trajectory "we cannot rule out catastrophic outcomes where human life as we know it is threatened".  JPMorgan subsequently distanced itself from the content of the study.<sup id="cite_ref-greenfield-and-watts-2020_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greenfield-and-watts-2020-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Offices">Offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Offices" data-section="43" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<p>Although the old <a href="/wiki/Chase_Manhattan_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Chase Manhattan Bank">Chase Manhattan Bank</a>'s headquarters were located at <b>One Chase Manhattan Plaza</b> (now known as <a href="/wiki/28_Liberty_Street" title="28 Liberty Street">28 Liberty Street</a>) in downtown <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, the current temporary world headquarters for JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co. are located at <a href="/wiki/383_Madison_Avenue" title="383 Madison Avenue">383 Madison Avenue</a>. In 2018, JPMorgan announced they would demolish the current headquarters building at <a href="/wiki/270_Park_Avenue" title="270 Park Avenue">270 Park Avenue</a>, which was <a href="/wiki/Union_Carbide" title="Union Carbide">Union Carbide</a>'s former headquarters, to make way for a newer building that will be 500 feet (150 m) taller than the existing building. Demolition is expected to begin in early 2019, and the new building will be completed in 2025. The replacement 70-story headquarters will be able to fit 15,000 employees, whereas the current building fits 6,000 employees in a space that has a capacity of 3,500. The new headquarters is part of the East Midtown rezoning plan.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> When construction is completed in 2025, the headquarters will then move back into the new building at 270 Park Avenue.
</p><p>The bulk of North American operations take place in four buildings located adjacent to each other on <a href="/wiki/Park_Avenue" title="Park Avenue">Park Avenue</a> in New York City: the former <a href="/wiki/Union_Carbide" title="Union Carbide">Union Carbide</a> Building at 270 Park Avenue, the hub of sales and trading operations (which is being demolished and replaced), and the original Chemical Bank building at <a href="/wiki/277_Park_Avenue" title="277 Park Avenue">277 Park Avenue</a>, where most investment banking activity takes place. Asset and wealth management groups are located at <a href="/wiki/245_Park_Avenue" title="245 Park Avenue">245 Park Avenue</a> and <a href="/wiki/345_Park_Avenue" title="345 Park Avenue">345 Park Avenue</a>. Other groups are located in the former Bear Stearns building at <a href="/wiki/383_Madison_Avenue" title="383 Madison Avenue">383 Madison Avenue</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Chase_bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Chase bank">Chase</a>, the U.S. and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, retail, commercial, and credit card bank is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Chase_Tower_(Chicago)" title="Chase Tower (Chicago)">Chase Tower</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JPMH_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JPMH-9">[9]</a></sup></p><p>The Asia Pacific headquarters for JPMorgan is located in <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> at <a href="/wiki/Chater_House" title="Chater House">Chater House</a>.
</p><p>Approximately 11,050 employees are located in <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus</a> at <a href="/wiki/McCoy_Building" class="mw-redirect" title="McCoy Building">the McCoy Center</a>, the former <a href="/wiki/Bank_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank One">Bank One</a> offices. The building is the largest JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co. facility in the world and the second largest single-tenant office building in the United States behind <a href="/wiki/The_Pentagon" title="The Pentagon">The Pentagon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dispatch_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dispatch-148">[148]</a></sup></p><p>The bank moved some of its operations to the <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase_Tower_(Houston)" title="JPMorgan Chase Tower (Houston)">JPMorgan Chase Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston</a>, when it purchased <a href="/wiki/Texas_Commerce_Bank" title="Texas Commerce Bank">Texas Commerce Bank</a>.
</p>

		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px"><div style="width: 235px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 230px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:25_Bank_Street_2012.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/25_Bank_Street_2012.JPG/79px-25_Bank_Street_2012.JPG" decoding="async" width="79" height="135" data-file-width="2152" data-file-height="3649"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 79px;height: 135px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/25_Bank_Street_2012.JPG/79px-25_Bank_Street_2012.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="79" data-height="135"> </span></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/25_Bank_Street" title="25 Bank Street">25 Bank Street</a><br>London, United Kingdom
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul><p>The Global Corporate Bank's main headquarters are in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, with regional headquarters in Hong Kong, New York and <a href="/wiki/Sao_Paulo" class="mw-redirect" title="Sao Paulo">Sao Paulo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p><p>The Card Services division has its headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Wilmington,_Delaware" title="Wilmington, Delaware">Wilmington, Delaware</a>, with Card Services offices in <a href="/wiki/Elgin,_Illinois" title="Elgin, Illinois">Elgin, Illinois</a>; <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Missouri" title="Springfield, Missouri">Springfield, Missouri</a>; <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="San Antonio, Texas">San Antonio, Texas</a>; <a href="/wiki/Mumbai,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbai, India">Mumbai, India</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Cebu_City" title="Cebu City">Cebu, Philippines</a>.
</p><p>Additional large operation centers are located in <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>; <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles, California">Los Angeles, California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newark,_Delaware" title="Newark, Delaware">Newark, Delaware</a>; <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando, Florida</a>; <a href="/wiki/Tampa,_Florida" title="Tampa, Florida">Tampa, Florida</a>; <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis,_Indiana" class="mw-redirect" title="Indianapolis, Indiana">Indianapolis, Indiana</a>; <a href="/wiki/Louisville,_Kentucky" title="Louisville, Kentucky">Louisville, Kentucky</a>; <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn,_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn, New York">Brooklyn, New York</a>; <a href="/wiki/Rochester,_New_York" title="Rochester, New York">Rochester, New York</a>; <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus, Ohio</a>; <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas, Texas</a>; <a href="/wiki/Fort_Worth,_Texas" title="Fort Worth, Texas">Fort Worth, Texas</a>; <a href="/wiki/Plano,_Texas" title="Plano, Texas">Plano, Texas</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee,_Wisconsin" class="mw-redirect" title="Milwaukee, Wisconsin">Milwaukee, Wisconsin</a>.
</p><p>Operation centers in Canada are located in <a href="/wiki/Burlington,_Ontario" title="Burlington, Ontario">Burlington, Ontario</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto, Ontario</a>.
</p><p>Operations centers in the United Kingdom are located in Bournemouth, Glasgow, London, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swindon" title="Swindon">Swindon</a>. The London location also serves as the European headquarters.
</p><p>Additional offices and technology operations are located in <a href="/wiki/Manila,_Philippines" class="mw-redirect" title="Manila, Philippines">Manila, Philippines</a>; <a href="/wiki/Cebu_City" title="Cebu City">Cebu, Philippines</a>; <a href="/wiki/Mumbai,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Mumbai, India">Mumbai, India</a>; <a href="/wiki/Bangalore,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangalore, India">Bangalore, India</a>; <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyderabad, India">Hyderabad, India</a>; <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi,_India" class="mw-redirect" title="New Delhi, India">New Delhi, India</a>; <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires,_Argentina" class="mw-redirect" title="Buenos Aires, Argentina">Buenos Aires, Argentina</a>; <a href="/wiki/Sao_Paulo,_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Sao Paulo, Brazil">Sao Paulo, Brazil</a>; <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City,_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexico City, Mexico">Mexico City, Mexico</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem,_Israel" class="mw-redirect" title="Jerusalem, Israel">Jerusalem, Israel</a>.
</p><p>In the late autumn of 2017, JPMorgan Chase opened a new global operations center in <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Credit_derivatives">Credit derivatives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Credit derivatives" data-section="44" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<p>The derivatives team at JPMorgan (including <a href="/wiki/Blythe_Masters" title="Blythe Masters">Blythe Masters</a>) was a pioneer in the invention of <a href="/wiki/Credit_derivative" title="Credit derivative">credit derivatives</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Credit_default_swap" title="Credit default swap">credit default swap</a>. The first CDS was created to allow <a href="/wiki/Exxon" title="Exxon">Exxon</a> to borrow money from JPMorgan while JPMorgan transferred the risk to the <a href="/wiki/European_Bank_of_Reconstruction_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="European Bank of Reconstruction and Development">European Bank of Reconstruction and Development</a>. JPMorgan's team later created the 'BISTRO', a bundle of credit default swaps that was the progenitor of the <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_CDO" title="Synthetic CDO">Synthetic CDO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> As of 2013 JPMorgan had the largest credit default swap and credit derivatives portfolio by total notional amount of any US bank.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Multibillion-dollar_trading_loss">Multibillion-dollar trading loss</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Multibillion-dollar trading loss" data-section="45" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2012_JPMorgan_Chase_trading_loss" title="2012 JPMorgan Chase trading loss">2012 JPMorgan Chase trading loss</a></div>
<p>In April 2012, hedge fund insiders became aware that the market in credit default swaps was possibly being affected by the activities of <a href="/wiki/2012_JPMorgan_Chase_trading_loss" title="2012 JPMorgan Chase trading loss">Bruno Iksil</a>, a trader for JPMorgan Chase &amp; Co., referred to as "the London whale" in reference to the huge positions he was taking. Heavy opposing bets to his positions are known to have been made by traders, including another branch of J.P. Morgan, who purchased the derivatives offered by J.P. Morgan in such high volume.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTLR_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTLR-156">[156]</a></sup> Early reports were denied and minimized by the firm in an attempt to minimize exposure.<sup id="cite_ref-DealPP_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DealPP-157">[157]</a></sup> Major losses, $2 billion, were reported by the firm in May 2012, in relation to these trades and updated to $4.4 billion on July 13, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT071312_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT071312-158">[158]</a></sup> The disclosure, which resulted in headlines in the media, did not disclose the exact nature of the trading involved, which remains in progress and as of June 28, 2012, was continuing to produce losses which could total as much as $9 billion under worst-case scenarios.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT62812_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT62812-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DealBookUp_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DealBookUp-160">[160]</a></sup> The item traded, possibly related to CDX IG 9, <a href="/wiki/Credit_default_swap_index" title="Credit default swap index">an index based on the default risk</a> of major U.S. corporations,<sup id="cite_ref-WSJwaves_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJwaves-161">[161]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eFN_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eFN-162">[162]</a></sup> has been described as a "derivative of a derivative".<sup id="cite_ref-DNBlack_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DNBlack-163">[163]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DealBook2B_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DealBook2B-164">[164]</a></sup> On the company's emergency conference call, JPMorgan Chase Chairman, CEO and President Jamie Dimon said the strategy was "flawed, complex, poorly reviewed, poorly executed, and poorly monitored".<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> The episode is being investigated by the Federal Reserve, the SEC, and the FBI.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable sortable floatright"><caption>Fines levied regarding the 2012 JPMorgan Chase trading loss<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_whale1_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_whale1-167">[167]</a></sup></caption>
<tbody><tr><th>Regulator</th>
<th>Nation</th>
<th>Fine
</th></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_Comptroller_of_the_Currency" title="Office of the Comptroller of the Currency">Office of the Comptroller of the Currency</a></td>
<td rowspan="3">US</td>
<td>$300m
</td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Securities and Exchange Commission">Securities and Exchange Commission</a></td>
<td>$200m
</td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/US_Federal_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="US Federal Reserve">Federal Reserve</a></td>
<td>$200m
</td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Financial_Conduct_Authority" title="Financial Conduct Authority">Financial Conduct Authority</a></td>
<td>UK</td>
<td>£138m ($221m US)
</td></tr></tbody></table><p>On September 18, 2013, JPMorgan Chase agreed to pay a total of $920 million in fines and penalties to American and UK regulators for violations related to the trading loss and other incidents. The fine was part of a multiagency and multinational settlement with the Federal Reserve, <a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_Comptroller_of_the_Currency" title="Office of the Comptroller of the Currency">Office of the Comptroller of the Currency</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Securities and Exchange Commission">Securities and Exchange Commission</a> in the United States and the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Conduct_Authority" title="Financial Conduct Authority">Financial Conduct Authority</a> in the UK. The company also admitted breaking American securities law.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> The fines amounted to the third biggest banking fine levied by US regulators, and the second largest by UK authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_whale1_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_whale1-167">[167]</a></sup> As of September 19, 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, two traders face criminal proceedings.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_whale1_167-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_whale1-167">[167]</a></sup> It is also the first time in several years that a major American financial institution has publicly admitted breaking the securities laws.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup></p><p>A report by the SEC was critical of the level of oversight from senior management on traders, and the FCA said the incident demonstrated "flaws permeating all levels of the firm: from portfolio level right up to senior management."<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_whale1_167-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_whale1-167">[167]</a></sup></p><p>On the day of the fine, the BBC reported from the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a> that the fines "barely registered" with traders there, the news having been an expected development and the company having prepared for the financial hit.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_whale1_167-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_whale1-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_collection">Art collection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Art collection" data-section="46" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/J._P._Morgan#Collector_of_art,_books,_and_gemstones" title="J. P. Morgan">J. P. Morgan § Collector of art, books, and gemstones</a></div>
<p>The collection was begun in 1959 by <a href="/wiki/David_Rockefeller" title="David Rockefeller">David Rockefeller</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> and comprises over 30,000 objects, of which over 6,000 are photographic-based,<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> as of 2012 containing more than one hundred works by Middle Eastern and North African artists.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> The One Chase Manhattan Plaza building was the original location at the start of collection by the Chase Manhattan Bank, the current collection containing both this and also those works that the First National Bank of Chicago had acquired prior to assimilation into the JPMorgan Chase organization.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> L. K. Erf has been the director of acquisitions of works since 2004 for the bank,<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> whose art program staff is completed by an additional three full-time members and one registrar.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> The advisory committee at the time of the Rockefeller initiation included <a href="/wiki/Alfred_H._Barr,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Alfred H. Barr, Jr.">A. H. Barr</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Canning_Miller" title="Dorothy Canning Miller">D. Miller</a>, and also J. J. Sweeney, R. Hale, P. Rathbone and G. Bunshaft.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(11)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_sponsorships">Major sponsorships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Major sponsorships" data-section="47" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-11 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-11">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Chase_Field" title="Chase Field">Chase Field</a>, (formerly Bank One Ballpark) <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>, – <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Diamondbacks" title="Arizona Diamondbacks">Arizona Diamondbacks</a>, <a href="/wiki/MLB" class="mw-redirect" title="MLB">MLB</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chase_Center_(San_Francisco)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chase Center (San Francisco)">Chase Center (San Francisco)</a> - <a href="/wiki/Golden_State_Warriors" title="Golden State Warriors">Golden State Warriors</a>, <a href="/wiki/NBA" class="mw-redirect" title="NBA">NBA</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a></li>
<li>Chase Auditorium (formerly Bank One Auditorium) inside of <a href="/wiki/Chase_Tower_(Chicago)" title="Chase Tower (Chicago)">Chase Tower (Chicago)</a> (formerly Bank One Tower)</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase_Corporate_Challenge" class="mw-redirect" title="JPMorgan Chase Corporate Challenge">JPMorgan Chase Corporate Challenge</a>, owned and operated by JPMorgan Chase, is the largest corporate road racing series in the world with over 200,000 participants in 12 cities in six countries on five continents. It has been held annually since 1977 and the races range in size from 4,000 entrants to more than 60,000.</li>
<li>JPMorgan Chase is the official sponsor of the <a href="/wiki/US_Open_(tennis)" title="US Open (tennis)">US Open</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/J.P._Morgan_Asset_Management" class="mw-redirect" title="J.P. Morgan Asset Management">J.P. Morgan Asset Management</a> is the Principal Sponsor of the <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">English</a> Premiership Rugby 7s Series.</li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(12)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership">Leadership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Leadership" data-section="48" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-12 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-12">
<p>Jamie Dimon is the Chairman and CEO of JPMorgan Chase. The acquisition deal of Bank One in 2004, was designed in part to recruit Dimon to JPMorgan Chase. He became chief executive at the end of 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> Dimon has been recognized for his leadership during the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007–2008">2008 financial crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> Under his leadership, JPMorgan Chase rescued two ailing banks during the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> Although Dimon has publicly criticized the American government's strict immigration policies,<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> as of July 2018, his company has $1.6 million worth of stocks in Sterling Construction (the company contracted to build a massive wall on the U.S.-Mexico border).<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(13)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_former_employees">Notable former employees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Notable former employees" data-section="49" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-13 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-13">
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. <ul><li><a href="/wiki/Winthrop_Aldrich" class="mw-redirect" title="Winthrop Aldrich">Winthrop Aldrich</a> – son of the late Senator <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Aldrich" class="mw-redirect" title="Nelson Aldrich">Nelson Aldrich</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andrew_Crockett_(British_banker)" class="mw-redirect" title="Andrew Crockett (British banker)">Andrew Crockett</a> – former general manager of the <a href="/wiki/Bank_for_International_Settlements" title="Bank for International Settlements">Bank for International Settlements</a> (1994–2003)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pierre_Danon" title="Pierre Danon">Pierre Danon</a> – chairman of <a href="/wiki/Eircom" class="mw-redirect" title="Eircom">Eircom</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dina_Dublon" title="Dina Dublon">Dina Dublon</a> – member of the board of directors of <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accenture" title="Accenture">Accenture</a> and <a href="/wiki/PepsiCo" title="PepsiCo">PepsiCo</a> and former Executive Vice President and Chief Financial Officer of JPMorgan Chase</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Maria_Elena_Lagomasino" title="Maria Elena Lagomasino">Maria Elena Lagomasino</a> – member of the board of directors of <a href="/wiki/The_Coca-Cola_Company" title="The Coca-Cola Company">The Coca-Cola Company</a> and former CEO of JPMorgan Private Bank</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jacob_A._Frenkel" title="Jacob A. Frenkel">Jacob A. Frenkel</a> – Governor of the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Israel" title="Bank of Israel">Bank of Israel</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_W._Lamont" title="Thomas W. Lamont">Thomas W. Lamont</a> – acting head of <a href="/wiki/J.P._Morgan_%26_Co." title="J.P. Morgan &amp; Co.">J.P. Morgan &amp; Co.</a> on <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929" title="Wall Street Crash of 1929">Black Tuesday</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_I._Lipp" title="Robert I. Lipp">Robert I. Lipp</a> – former CEO of <a href="/wiki/The_Travelers_Companies" title="The Travelers Companies">The Travelers Companies</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marjorie_Magner" title="Marjorie Magner">Marjorie Magner</a> – chairman of <a href="/wiki/Gannett_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Gannett Company">Gannett Company</a><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Henry_S._Morgan" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry S. Morgan">Henry S. Morgan</a> – co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">Morgan Stanley</a>, son of <a href="/wiki/J._P._Morgan,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="J. P. Morgan, Jr.">J. P. Morgan, Jr.</a> and grandson of financier <a href="/wiki/J._P._Morgan" title="J. P. Morgan">J. P. Morgan</a></li>
<li>Lewis Reford – Canadian political candidate</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/David_Rockefeller" title="David Rockefeller">David Rockefeller</a> – patriarch of the <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_family" title="Rockefeller family">Rockefeller family</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harold_Stanley" title="Harold Stanley">Harold Stanley</a> – former JPMorgan partner, co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">Morgan Stanley</a></li>
<li>Jan Stenbeck – former owner of <a href="/wiki/Investment_AB_Kinnevik" class="mw-redirect" title="Investment AB Kinnevik">Investment AB Kinnevik</a> [worked at Morgan Stanley but not JP Morgan; see Jan's Wikipedia page]</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Don_M._Wilson_III" title="Don M. Wilson III">Don M. Wilson III</a> – former <a href="/wiki/Chief_Risk_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Risk Officer">Chief Risk Officer</a> (CRO) of J. P. Morgan and current member of the board of directors at <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Montreal" title="Bank of Montreal">Bank of Montreal</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Charlie_Scharf&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Charlie Scharf (page does not exist)">Charlie Scharf</a>, current CEO of <a href="/wiki/Visa_Inc." title="Visa Inc.">Visa</a></li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_public_service">Politics and public service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Politics and public service" data-section="51" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Ma" title="Frederick Ma">Frederick Ma</a> – Hong Kong Secretary for Commerce and Economic Development (2007–08)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a> – <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a> (1997–2007)<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/William_M._Daley" title="William M. Daley">William M. Daley</a> – U.S. Secretary of Commerce (1997–2000), U.S. White House Chief of Staff (2011–2012)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Forsyth,_Baron_Forsyth_of_Drumlean" title="Michael Forsyth, Baron Forsyth of Drumlean">Michael Forsyth, Baron Forsyth of Drumlean</a> – Secretary of State for Scotland (1995–97)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_S._Gates,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas S. Gates, Jr.">Thomas S. Gates, Jr.</a> – U.S. Secretary of Defense (1959–61)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/David_Laws" title="David Laws">David Laws</a> – UK <a href="/wiki/Chief_Secretary_to_the_Treasury" title="Chief Secretary to the Treasury">Chief Secretary to the Treasury</a> (May 2010) Minister of State for Schools</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rick_Lazio" title="Rick Lazio">Rick Lazio</a> – member of the U.S. House of Representatives (1993–2001)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Antony_Leung" title="Antony Leung">Antony Leung</a> – Financial Secretary of Hong Kong (2001–03)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dwight_Morrow" title="Dwight Morrow">Dwight Morrow</a> – U.S. Senator (1930–31)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Margaret_Ng" title="Margaret Ng">Margaret Ng</a> – member of the Hong Kong Legislative Council</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/George_P._Shultz" class="mw-redirect" title="George P. Shultz">George P. Shultz</a> – U.S. Secretary of Labor (1969–70), U.S. Secretary of Treasury (1972–74), U.S. Secretary of State (1982–89)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_J._McCloy" title="John J. McCloy">John J. McCloy</a> - president of the World Bank, U.S. High Commissioner for Germany, chairman of Chase Manhattan Bank, chairman of the Council on Foreign Relations, a member of the Warren Commission, and a prominent United States adviser to all presidents from Franklin D. Roosevelt to Ronald Reagan.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mahua_Moitra" title="Mahua Moitra">Mahua Moitra</a> - Indian Member of Parliament, Lok Sabha.</li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=JPMorgan_Chase&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Other" data-section="52" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
